GT Equivalence Verification (CRK30)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A - c1*A*exp(-c2*_s*t) + c3*_t*sin(log(A + c4))
Candidates evaluated: 55
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to analyze whether any candidate can exactly match the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.25667*A - 0.25667*A*exp(-0.02054*t) + 0.94264*sin(log(A + 1))`

The key components of the GT are:
1. A linear term in A
2. A term `A*exp(-αt)` (exponential decay in t, multiplied by A)
3. A `sin(log(A + 1))` term

The `sin(log(A+1))` term is crucial. This is a very specific transcendental function that cannot be represented by:
- Polynomials in A
- Exponentials `exp(A*c)`
- Rational functions like `A/(cA+1)^2` or `A/(c+A)`
- `log(A*c+1)` alone
- Power functions `A^c`
- `log(A²*c+1)/A^(1/3)`

Let me check each candidate for the presence of `sin(log(...))` or equivalent:

**Scanning all 55 candidates:** None of them contain `sin()` or any trigonometric function. They all use combinations of:
- Linear terms in A
- `exp(A*c)` terms
- `exp(c*t)*Max(0,A)` terms (which can match `A*exp(-αt)`)
- Rational functions: `A/(cA+1)^2`, `A/(c+A)`, `1/(cA+1)^2`, `1/(c+A)`
- `log(A*c+1)` terms
- Power terms `A^c`, `A²`
- `log(A²*c+1)/A^(1/3)` terms
- `t` terms, `t^c` terms, `log(c*t+1)` terms
- `1/A`, `1/A²` terms

The GT contains `sin(log(A+1))`, which is an oscillatory function in `log(A+1)`. None of the basis functions in any candidate are oscillatory. By the principle of linear independence of basis functions (Rule 3), no combination of the non-oscillatory functions listed above can exactly equal `sin(log(A+1))` for all values of A ≥ 0.

Therefore, **no candidate can match the GT**.
